# Definitions

Definitions are extracted verbatim where pattern matching identified definition-style sentences. Verify formal quotations against the source PDF.

## A (free) tree T

- a simple graph such that if u and v are two vertices in T, there is a unique path from u to v.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Minimum Spanning Tree](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/10-8-minimum-spanning-tree.md)
- a simple graph such that if u and v are two vertices in T, there is a unique path from u to v.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Breadth-First Topological Ordering](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/10-10-breadth-first-topological-ordering.md)
## A binary tree

- a dynamic data structure; that is, memory for its nodes is allocated and deallocated during program execution.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Binary Trees](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/9-1-binary-trees.md)
## A call to this function

- as follows: heapify(list, 0, 9); We thus obtain the binary tree as shown in Figure 8-48(c).  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Heapsort: Array-Based Lists](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/8-5-heapsort-array-based-lists.md)
## A candidate key

- any field or combination of fields that could potentially be used as the primary key in a table.  
  Source: Information Systems 622 Study Guide, [Definitions](../documents/information-systems-622-study-guide/sections/3-4-1-definitions.md)
## A circuit

- a path of nonzero length from a vertex u to u with no repeated edges.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Breadth-First Topological Ordering](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/10-10-breadth-first-topological-ordering.md)
## A class

- a collection of a fixed number of components.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Classes](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/1-4-classes.md)
- a collection of a fixed number of components.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Identifying Classes, Objects, and Operations](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/1-7-identifying-classes-objects-and-operations.md)

- accessed using the class variable name, followed by the dot operator (.  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Identifying Classes, Objects, and Operations](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/1-7-identifying-classes-objects-and-operations.md)

## A graph G

  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Graph Definitions and Notations](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/10-2-graph-definitions-and-notations.md)

## A heap

- a list in which each element contains a key, such that the key in the element at position k in the list is at least as large as the key in the element at position 2k + 1 (if it exists) and 2k + 2 (if it exists).  
  Source: Programming 622 Study Guide, [Heapsort: Array-Based Lists](../documents/programming-622-study-guide/sections/8-5-heapsort-array-based-lists.md)

## A tree T

- called a spanning tree of graph G if T is a subgraph of G such that V(T) = V(G), that is, all the vertices of G are in T.
